RATING: 7
Having good art doesn't make a game automatically similar to Dixit. They're not. They play Completely differently. 

Dixit offers rich creative freedom, Mysterium doesn't at all. Mysterium is like the voting part of Dixit without the storyteling. And that's okay. But here the similarity ends. 

Mysterium offers a strong cooperative feel, somehow perfectly mixed with the sense of individuality. 
"Yes, we all just won, but... did we? The three of Us voted correctly in the end, not you two! And from us, these two had the highest score on the track so they are the ultimate winners!"
Obviously, all that really matters is that we all won, but the possibility of a victory within victory enriches the game and was implemented so seamlessly.

RATING: 8
11/10/2017 - Raising rating because after a year of replays, the aforementioned time lag problem has become less and less of an issue. When I'm the ghost, I no longer have a problem even with the maximum player count. The trick is realizing that there won't be a perfect clue and settling for something that's good enough. I also have gotten quite good at saying, 'no good clue for this person, let's do the other people first' so as to not freeze up. I've noticed that other experienced ghosts play similarly. Also, I've added a little bit of extra spice to the second half of the game by asking people to describe the murder. Overall, this has improved the game a great deal, and has allowed it to stay. Plus, few games are so fantastic for Halloween.

07/25/2016 - Great game with 2-4 players, but when I played with 7, the 'time lag' of the ghost's decision-making becomes considerable and the game moves too slowly. May still work in a large group of friends, but for a typical game night group of people, plays better with less people.

RATING: 8
Dixit left me cold, but this game is great. One player (the ghost) tries to refer pictures of persons, places and items with other, more abstract pictures (dreams). Other players, the investigaters try to find out the connections. Engaging, beautiful, original, cooperative and rather fast, at least with 4 players. I read, that it is suggested that with 6-7 players, the group should split into 2 groups which seems to be a reasonable idea. The game components make it possible (unintetionally).

RATING: 7.55
A very unique game, albeit one that potentially suffers from meta-game analysis a little too much.   

The gist of the game is that the "ghost" provides hints to a player about a person/place/object related to a murder through the use of dream cards that, smartly, have the potential to refer to lots of different persons/places/objects.  Over repeated plays, I could see it becoming problematic that a player might know that a particular ghost player always uses color schemes as the defining characteristic of his or her hints, etc.  That said, the limited hand of cards that the ghost player has to work with will at times mitigate even this potential problem.  

With a group of relatively non-serious gamers, I found the regular difficulty level of this game about right.  On all three games, the final round was reached, but not always with the psychics making the correct final guess.

RATING: 9
[GAMEID=39856] with a purpose.  Thrives and suffers for the same reasons but more so.

Thrives:  Makes you think & draw connections.  Must be flexible and creative.  Not a serious game - play it for fun, for the experience.

Suffers:  Clue cards can be rough at times.  Definitely not for everyone.  Can be frustrating.

I like this one a lot.  It's a great later-in-the-night, non-serious game.  More experiential than anything, but the game elements are tight enough to establish purpose and benchmarks.  Difficulty is scalable (which is AWESOME).  Decent-to-good replay value.  Overall, absolutely perfect for what it's supposed to be.

I strongly suggest you try it and see if it's for you.

RATING: 8
Mysterium is really great and for someone like me, who studies translation and communication, it's also a fascinating experience. You have the information and you're trying to transmit it to the other players without talking... just using pictures. It's very interesting! Mysterium does also everything right to be a good cooperative game: it's tense, it's difficult and it has a very nice theme, but it also doesn't suffer of the aplha-gamer problem, because nobody can be 100% sure about the meaning of the dream cards. 

I also think that Mysterium is one of the best gateway games out there... way better than something like Ticket to Ride or other "classics" for a lot of reasons. It has simple rules and beautiful components like other games, but it also goes up to 7 players, it has the visual impact of Dixit and the basic concept of Clue, that a lot of people already know, and it's cooperative, which allows for a friendlier game-play and it's something completely new for those who only played Monopoly and Risk. I really can't think of any other game that would be better as a gateway experience!

Now the entire game was made even better with the new edition! The new components and arts are wonderful, but I'm particularly happy for the screen, which is what the game needed to flow more smoothly. I also like the changes to the rules, which is something I didn't expect going into the game. I wasn't sure about the hourglass, because I liked to have the possibility of a longer discussion, but it actually brought some tension, which I really enjoyed, and kept the game running at the right speed. Even less sure I felt about the clairvoyance tokens, but I was pleasantly surprised by them. I like how this addition brings new decisions to be made and gives you a sort of consolation prize, when you get your clue wrong but you can go up on the track, because you were right about something else. 

Overall an excellent and beautiful light cooperative game, that can be played with everybody and rarely fails to entertain.

Rating without expansion: 8

RATING: 7
1st plays: The kids absolutely loved this one.  I played some spooky haunted house music, lowered the lights and had them close their eyes while I handed out their "visions" to them.  They got into the theme and insisted we play a 2nd game right away.  My daughter insisted on being the ghost, and I think she did better than me.  The theme of this game really comes through, and the art is great.  An improvement on Dixit in every way.

2nd plays: Worked equally well a second time.  It is by no means a heavy game but it accomplishes what it sets out to do.  The theme is very rich and the excellent production completes the package.  The artwork in the game is well done and fits with the roles and locations.  The weapon cards are bit harder to tie together, as the weapon cards don't have much on them to connect with dream cards.  It seems like an intentional design choice and it forces you to try to solve the weapons in a different way than the other cards.

RATING: 5.5
I'm a bit conflicted on this one. I like the idea of using Dixit mechanisms to create a deduction-style game. But it ends up playing out more like a race game, and your ability to move forward really revolves around what cards the ghost was able to pull and how well they are able to indicate what they want you to pick, which would be good, if it was spread over a longer game, so that things can even out. But it's a surprisingly short game and it's probably about half as long as it would need to be to start evening things out.

I think that with a worse production, so that it looked and felt like a small game, this wouldn't bother me. But when you open the box and set everything up, it looks like you're about to start playing Dead of Winter or something. And then it ends up feeling more like you've played a half-round of Codenames. If the table presence felt like Codenames, that might not bother me. But with the overwrought production, it feels like it's all facade and very little game. If I was the one to buy the game, I'd feel a bit cheated. Even as a player, I still felt that way a little bit.

Most importantly, I just don't feel like the game had to be as short as it was. The developers could easily have added more options to search among, or more stages to go through. Or if they wanted it to be a small, tight game to go through a few half-dozen times in a row, they could have pared down the production, streamlined the rules a little bit, so that it was quicker to set up and tear through the game a few times. It's effectively Codenames. It should be as straightforward as Codenames.

Beyond that, there's the element of betting on who is right and who is wrong. This felt awkward. The game feels like it should be a cooperative title, but instead we have to wait until someone has bet to tell them that we think they are wrong. And if they are wrong, and wrong often, then we will have to wait for them to catch up, so that we can finish the game. If they don't then we will all lose to the clock.

I suppose that's one way that a semi-cooperative game works, but it doesn't feel natural, like being a hoarder in Dead of Winter or a traitor in Shadows Over Camelot. It prevents anyone from alpha gaming the other players, I suppose. But, like I said, it didn't feel natural.

The game doesn't suck. But it definitely feels like this isn't the game that it should be.

ETA: It sounds like the original rules for the game did not have the elements that I didn't like. You might try looking them up and giving them a try!

RATING: 7
Πανέμορφο συνεργατικό party game όπου ένας παίκτης αναλαμβάνει τον ρόλο ενός φαντάσματος που προσπαθεί να δώσει στους ντετεκτιβ να καταλάβουν ποιός είναι ο δολοφόνος. Και επειδή σαν φάντασμα δεν μπορεί να μιλήσει, προσπαθεί να επικοινωνήσει μαζί τους μέσω ονείρων. :p

Το φάντασμα λοιπόν μοιράζει κρυφά για κάθε παίκτη ένα δολοφόνο μια τοποθεσία και ένα όπλο. Όλες αυτές τις πληροφορίες τις κρατάει κρυφές πίσω από μια οθόνη. Κάθε γύρα δίνει σε κάθε παίκτη μια ή και παραπάνω κάρτες-ονειρα (σκεφτείτε ζωγραφιές στυλ dixit) και ο κάθε παίκτης προσπαθεί να βρει τον δολοφόνο που ανατέθηκε σε αυτόν ανάμεσα σε όλους τους υποπτους στο τραπέζι. Αν το βρει μετά προχωρά στη στην τοποθεσία και μετά στο όπλο. Μέσα σε 7 γύρους το πολύ πρέπει όλοι να τα βρούν όλα αλλιώς χάνουν. 

Υπάρχει και η τελική φάση όπου το φάντασμα διαλέγει κρυφά ποιανού παίκτη ο δολοφόνος είναι τελικά ο σωστός δολοφόνος και προσπαθεί με 3 κάρτες όνειρα να δώσει στους παίκτες να το καταλάβουν. Σε αυτή τη φάση η κάθε μια από τις 3 κάρτες δίνει στοιχείο για το πρόσωπο την τοποθεσία και το όπλο αλλά οι ντετεκτιβ δεν ξέρουν ποια κάρτα δείχνει τι. Οπότε το συζητάν και καταλήγουν όλοι μαζί κάπου και είτε κερδίζουν είτε χάνουν.   
     
Υπάρχουν και advanced κανόνες με τον κάθε παίκτη να μαζεύει VP ποντάροντας αν ο συμπαίκτης του κάνει λάθος ή σωστά αλλά τους βρίσκω πραγματικά ανούσιους και είναι εύκολο να τους κάνεις game. Κάτι σκηνικά του στιλ «παιδιά θα βάλω αυτή την λάθος απάντηση ώστε να ποντάρετε όλοι στο λάθος μου και να πάρετε VP» τα βρίσκω κόντρα στο πνεύμα του παιχνιδιού. :shake:

Πολύ καλό party game με φοβερό artwork και πολύ καλά components.

RATING: 7
Mysterium was a hit around the holidays with the extended family. Good for higher play counts of 5-7 players. It is quite easy to teach the basics of the game and dive into playing. 

For a couple of items holding this back from a higher rating: the rule book seems badly organized (we didn't get all the rules correct in our first couple of plays, mainly due to people wanting the game to keep moving and no one being completely familiar with some of the rule minutiae); and "winning" the game lacks a little pop (similar to Clue, it just ends on the reveal.

Edit, March 2017: Junk Art is the new party game for me, and I prefer other "gateway" weight games over this. 

Edit: May 2017: This is a keeper and will get played at play counts of 5-7. It's a good game. I look forward to seeing if the new expansion fixes my issues with the end game.

Promos/Extras/Expansions:
Mysterium: Hidden Signs (2016)
Mysterium: Secrets & Lies (2017)
Mysterium: Secrets & Lies – First Printing Promo (2017)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I remember playing the first Polish iteration of this game a few years ago at the Dice Tower Con and leaving with a feeling of "meh" after my play. Maybe it was the poor rules explanation leaving my co-players and I bewildered or the tiredness of a late night of a con, but having played the new version, Mysterium, the game went up a few notches in the totem pole. 

Don't get me wrong, these social experiment games are not really in my wheelhouse, but playing with the right group and understanding the rules fully made a big difference in my opinion of the game. 

Each player is trying to decipher a who, where and with what murder in order to get to the final whodunit. All of the players must find their objectives because, if not, everyone loses. The way the clues are given is via cards with different pictures, abstractions and paintings. They are given by a Ghost via his dreams who is trying to find who murdered him. Sometimes, the clues given do not make sense since the Ghost is limited to seven cards per clue and has to make the best choice among them. This makes for hilarious and fun times as well as interesting deduction moments. Because of certain rules in the game, the cooperation element is not really hindered by an alpha player like some other co-ops.

The production values are very good and the art on the cards is top notch. I wish the insert would fit sleeved cards... I'm glad to have this title in my repertoire since it scratches an itch not provided by the multitude of heavier Euro games in my collection.

*Disclaimer: The listed rating/10 is heavily weighted towards my enjoyment of the game and the experience that it provides. Each pro and con are factored individually towards a cumulative score, but do not have fixed increments in which they can detract or increase a rating.

Pros:

+ Actually feels co-operative
+ Accommodating player count
+ Engrossing theme
+ Excelent Artwork and Components

- Too Fiddly

- Limited Replay Value

RATING: 3
Whilst many people praise the game for being Dixit "with a point", I personally find this actually makes Mysterium slightly too easy and significantly reduces its replayability. Whilst Dixit offers players the opportunity to find new and creative ways to play the same cards repeatedly, in Mysterium (after only five plays) playing the clue cards had already become entirely scripted within our group - i.e. specific cards had already come to represent specific people, rooms or weapons, meaning there was little choice for all the player. Very much enjoyed playing my first couple of games of this one, but it certainly wasn't the Dixit killer I expected. Rating reduced from 7.5 due to its limited replayability.

RATING: 8
I liked the idea of Dixit where you try to match rather "abstract" pictures to whatever you are trying to say. But doing this only to get points and to be the one with the most? Meh... isn't there something the same but different? Something with a twist?

Then somewhere somewhen Tajemnicze Domostwo showed up and sounded awesome. Although it was just in Polish I thought about getting it until I heard that it will be reprinted as Mysterium.

It is exactly what I expected and even more. This game is so much fun for either side. Trying to match the suspects to the dream-cards or the other way round while the psycists are guessing everything wrong. Even loosing is fun since you get to see the different aspects everybody was looking at.

I love it. A super cool party game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a solid game and a big hit over the holidays.  I played with my family and they loved this game.  Yes, it is Dixit meets Clue.  The production of the components is top notch.  They have card board clock to track roads.....very evocative and immersive.  The psychic figures are crystal balls which are awesome. There is a lot of attention to detail here.  I like the cartoony art personally.  It does not take away from the immersion for me that someone is a disembodied ghost and others are trying to catch a murderer.  I highly recommend this game if you liked Dixit.  This is not a Dixit killer.  It is a different game than Dixit.  My only complaint is that there are not a lot of murder weapon cards and I think after several plays the game will need an expansion. There are a lot of vision cards but again after repeated plays you will need an expansion.  Plenty of game in the box but if you play it a lot you will enjoy an expansion. Wait...one more complaint, there is one component (a extremely small token) to determine how "clairvoyant" a player is.  These tokens are entirely waaaaay too small and can be lost very easy.

Lo mejor es que es un juego cooperativo así que al final ganan o pierden todos juntos, aunque hay una pequeña recompensa a los que les va mejor en el transcurso de la partida.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I can't remember the last time I was so hyped for a game. I'm so happy this didn't disappoint! Basically what I'll say is that if you read the description and the game sounds fun to you, you're probably going to love it. It's just so clever and beautiful, I'm impressed on nearly every level.

It's funny that it ended up coming out so soon after Codenames in the U.S. - as a result every group I introduce this to immediately latches onto the "visual Codenames" description.

It's not a perfect game - it's true that the endgame can feel somewhat disconnected from the early game, but it's so much fun I'm really not bothered. Plus, if you're clever the early game really can make the difference as you build up a visual language for your clues.

So I accidentally played with the Ukranian rules first - as the 2 and 3p games are essentially those, and then when we first had a fourth person join at the end of a long night, we just stuck to those.

Finally got to try with the English rules though and I do like them, even if it feels a bit unnecessary. I kind of wish they were presented as the 'advanced rules' or something, just because I can definitely foresee myself playing by the Ukranian rules in certain situations still. But I think we will default to the English rules. The clairvoyance track rewards you for doing well in the early game, which makes the end game feel a bit more connected.

And even though it definitely feels arbitrary, doing the silent vote at the end is exciting. Getting to talk it all out with your friends as per the Ukranian rules is obviously enjoyable too, though.

The only true downside here is that it's a very content-driven game, so it doesn't take long to start seeing all the same stuff. Not the end of the world, but expansions will help give us the long tail here.

RATING: 7
Generates a lot of fun discussion between the players, in a way that Dixit never really accomplished when I played. There are a lot of fun misunderstandings from the ghost to the players. 

It is a little bit rules-heavy and fiddly for casual players, which limits this for me, but there are a couple of situations where it works. 

There are only 18 cards of each type. That is SEVERELY limiting. The dream cards - you could use Dixit cards to add to those. But the actual person/location/weapon cards are the issue. Played twice and already saw many duplicates, which allows visual cues and language to persist over games - for this game that is a huge downside, and is actually enough to turn this from an instant purchase to a no for me.

RATING: 9
Oh, loads of fun here! Very similar to Dixit in the way of forcing meaning from artwork. I'm certain these kinks grow out (and possibly grow tiresome) as the players memorize the card images. Also challenging to teach the game to new players while also playing the ghost at the same time.. this game definitely benefits from having at least two experienced players, one to be ghost and another to explain and maintain the board bits. In the end, absolutely worth it.

RATING: 7.5
Great game that suffers from minor faults, in my mind. Very easy to learn, incredible art, and fun theme. I think several of the cardboard components are unnecessary and could be left out or simplified; they only serve to make setup slower or, in the case of the tiny clairvoyance track markers, become lost... Overall, the greatest flaw of this game is the pacing, which scales to the number of players. Each turn, the ghost works through their vision cards for each player, during which time everyone else just sits around waiting. By contrast, the other players end up having a much faster, simultaneous turn. With 7 people playing, this game ends up being really boring for some people who need to stay engaged. At 4 people, the game proceeds relatively quickly. I think that there should be a way to force the ghost to pick cards faster, say 30 secs or 1 minute per player to dish out all vision cards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
Mysterium aka "Dixit - The Game" adds meaning and agency to the "ambigous pretty cards" mechanic popularized by Dixit. The theme lends itself well to light roll-playing (I'd advice some spooky moaning and floating around the table as the ghost) and atmosphere and the cooperative deduction approach of mysterium works just as well as Dixit's match-the-clue mechanic. The ability/need to guide players to certain cards over multiple rounds keeps everyone engaged and enables some light deduction. Pace is highly dependend on the ghost, who's task is decidedly more sophisticated  than those of the other players. As with all "restricted communication" games, groups need to figure out what flies with them and what doesn't, adding another layer of possible difficulty adjustment.

RATING: 7
Components: Gorgeous artwork, especialy on the character and location cards, and the ghost screen. The ghost cards are very Dixit-like; so much so that I think the Dixit cards could be used to expand this game.

Experience: As a ghost, very interesting. The cards are very limited, and send really ambiguous messages, so it's fun to try to play these wisely, and then see how they are interpreted.

Seems like it would be really tough to get high on the clairvoyance track. In our first game, noone made it past the first section, and so everyone had to guess the identity based on a singled revealed card.

The ghost is at a bit of a disadvantage if only looking at the cards behind the screen, as the clues might be better matches for the dummy suspect/location/weapon cards out on the table.

First Played: 2016-01-09
Last Played: 2016-02-10
Plays (2):
5 players: 2

Vous aimez DIXIT ? Vous aimez les enquêtes style CLUEDO ? Vous allez adorer Mysterium ! Vous êtes de vrais médiums. Et vous devez retrouver les éléments d'un meurtre. Est-ce le colonel Moutarde qui a commis le meurtre dans le petit salon avec un chandelier ? Hummmm ... Pour cela, le fantôme va vous aider : "Toc toc, Fantôme, es-tu là ?" Mais comme il ne peut pas parler (c'est un fantôme), il va vous envoyer des visions sous forme d'images : "Je vois...je vois .... un bateau dans une baignoire ...". Est-ce que cela veut dire que le meurtre a eu lieu dans une fontaine ? ou dans un endroit clos ? Mystèèèèrreeeee !  Mysterium est un jeu coopératif ! Tous ensemble pour comprendre les visions du fantôme. Il faudra bien ça ! Une ambiance de jeu sombre (mais pas oppressante), un jeu très bien illustré, saurez-vous lire à travers les images ? (Dans la boîte, il ne manque que la cape pour celui qui joue le fantôme... dommage :) )

Pour 2 à 7 joueurs, pour des parties de 42 minutes (après, le fantôme, il disparaît)

RATING: 8
A friend once described it to me as "spooky Dixit", which I found pretty apt. 

When I first played Mysterium, I did not enjoy it much, finding it sort of frustrating. This, fortunately, turned out to be because I was playing it with the wrong crowd. When I played again with players who were keenly invested in who the murderer could be and understood that you're supposed to be working as a team, Mysterium leaped up the ranks for me.

I have only managed to win Mysterium once - it is a tough game even when everyone is working together, Nonetheless, I have enjoyed it almost every time I have played. There's a lot of fun in trying to puzzle out the images provided by the ghost (OR, as the ghost, desperately trying to get people back on track as they stubbornly cling to the one aspect of the picture you didn't consider). The time limit can be stressful, but in a way that encourages cooperation. Overall, it's a fun, unique little game that I don't think everyone will like, but those who do like it will love it.

RATING: 6.7
One player takes on the role of a ghost of someone who has been killed, and tries to give clues to the other players in order for them to figure out who, where and with what object he was killed. In stage 1 all players have to find their own suspect, place and object. If all have succeeded in doing so after 7 rounds max, then stage 2 can start. All players can then vote for one of the suspects, after they have received some extra clues (at least if they were able to earn these extra clues during stage 1 by voting on the correct nature of the other players' choices as they were trying to figure out who, where and by which means their suspect alledgedly did it).

RATING: 7
Another of the new crop of fresh, innovative games. Players have a limited number of guesses at clue-like murder (culprit, weapon, & location).

The challenge is in trying to read into the images for the intention of the clue-giver. What pictures on this card associate with the suspects and locations?

RATING: 8.8
Probably my favorite game for non-board gamers. A game of deduction (and funky deduction at that), you have one player as the ghost giving very abstract clues to the other players to determine who killed them, where, and with what. The more "clairvoyant" you are at picking up on the ghost's clues, the better at the end. However the game is mostly cooperative.

It's a game that doesn't require much board game strategy to know how to play, what's most important is knowing what kind of person the ghost is, and how they think (though often they get screwed over with bad cards to give out). It does take a little while to setup, but of all the people I've played with, ~15 now, only one person has it really backfired on since they just didn't care.

I’ve never played ‘the ghost’ and honestly, after looking at all the preparation and rules consultation they do, don’t really have any desire to; it seems like a lot of effort for such little return. I still prefer Dixit a lot more to this game because in Dixit you are an acting participant (each and every person), yet here (unless you are the ‘ghost’) we are just re-acting to what is presented to us. RATING: 4
2016-02-06 : A game where the design intention clearly was to take a witty, quick-playing great game like Dixit and turn it into something less good. For starters : in Dixit you both are the clue giver and taker at various parts of the game, and that's fun. Clearly too much fun, so cut-out half of that experience. In Dixit there's very little downtime, and when there is some, you use it to come up with clever clues. Here the game is nothing but downtime waiting for the one GM to come-up with clues for everyone. In Dixit the most clever player wins. Can't have that, let's make it so that no matter how well you played this game, if in the end somebody else doesn't pick up on a clue, you lose. And in a 7-player game that's almost inevitable. This is simply a very badly designed totally over-hyped boring game

RATING: 8
Please note: despite there being English rules included with this edition of the game my comments are based on  the (I think) Ukrainian rules where the end game is trying to determine a person, place, and thing with exactly 3 clues. I do not play with this edition's bidding on people's guesses, the timer, and non-cooperative end game.

Lots of people have said this is co-op Clue meets Dixit. I would completely agree with this. Each round the ghost player silently gives Dixit-esque cards  to the other players. The players try to figure out which is their person/place/thing based on the strange card they've been given. Once they've figured out one of these, you move onto the next category. If all players get all of their people/places/things within a specified number of turns, there will be a final collective guess for which set among all of the players sets is actual circumstance of the ghosts murder based on exactly three dream cards the ghost provides as clues. This is extremely fun and is a great rules-light game that can be used as a gateway game. 

Gamers seem to like it a bit more than Dixit. I think many consider this to be a Dixit killer. I don't really agree, since they are pretty different (one is co-op and the other is competitive). I also think it's worthwhile to own both. I say this because the dream cards are so much like Dixit cards, I've used them in a game of Dixit and it worked well. I'm not sure if you could used Dixit cards as dream cards for Mysterium, but it might work. For me, the main reason one doesn't replace the other is that I like Dixit with 6+ players. With Mysterium, I'd rather play this with 3 - 5 players maximum. Why? The more players you play with, the more people/places/things are on display, making it harder to win. In addition, and probably more importantly, the more people you include, the longer it will take for the Ghost player to distribute dream cards and the more likely you are of going through the deck of dream cards (or seeing them more often making the game less replayable).

Regardless of what edition's rules you use, if someone is stuck on a person/place/thing, it can become apparent by round 6, that there is no chance of being able to do the Oneiromancy round. I think this takes away from the narrative arc of the game and is a bit anticlimactic.

RATING: 5
The game probably gets kudos for being the first in some genre, but at the point I finally had a chance to play the game there was nothing here I haven't experienced in other "guessing" party games. The artwork is top notch, the ghost screen is a very functional touch, and the sceance theme is a great fit. I do think the game tries to add too many fiddly rules which can complicate the game for some audiences, and in truth I believe takes away from the core fun inside (matching your Dixit art cards to the guesswork of the ghost player).

Two small design quibbles: why the decision to use a numbering system at the end of the game to reference the players, it would of made far more sense to simply use the player's color on the back of the voting tokens, and why were the weapon cards a different size?

RATING: 7
A Dixit killing machine. This takes one of my family's favorite party games (the aforementioned Dixit) and transforms it into an actual game. With essentially two games in one box (Ghost & Psychic) that feel surprisingly different, and varying difficulties, this is a great addition to any collection. Watching the psychics completely misconstrue your message is delightfully frustrating, and adapting to their train of thought is challenging and satisfying. The opposites are true when playing as a psychic. Its got more game than Dixit, and is more ambiguous than Codenames, making it a must own for the friendly cooperative gamer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
In the 1920s, Mr. MacDowell, a gifted astrologist, immediately detected a supernatural being upon entering his new house in Scotland. He gathered eminent mediums of his time for an extraordinary séance, and they have seven hours to contact the ghost and investigate any clues that it can provide to unlock an old mystery.

Unable to talk, the amnesic ghost communicates with the mediums through visions, which are represented in the game by illustrated cards. The mediums must decipher the images to help the ghost remember how he was murdered: Who did the crime? Where did it take place? Which weapon caused the death? The more the mediums cooperate and guess well, the easier it is to catch the right culprit.

In Mysterium, a reworking of the game system present in Tajemnicze Domostwo, one player takes the role of ghost while everyone else represents a medium. To solve the crime, the ghost must first recall (with the aid of the mediums) all of the suspects present on the night of the murder. A number of suspect, location and murder weapon cards are placed on the table, and the ghost randomly assigns one of each of these in secret to a medium.

Each hour (i.e., game turn), the ghost hands one or more vision cards face up to each medium, refilling their hand to seven each time they share vision cards. These vision cards present dreamlike images to the mediums, with each medium first needing to deduce which suspect corresponds to the vision cards received. Once the ghost has handed cards to the final medium, they start a two-minute sandtimer. Once a medium has placed their token on a suspect, they may also place clairvoyancy tokens on the guesses made by other mediums to show whether they agree or disagree with those guesses.

After time runs out, the ghost reveals to each medium whether the guesses were correct or not. Mediums who guessed correctly move on to guess the location of the crime (and then the murder weapon), while those who didn't keep their vision cards and receive new ones next hour corresponding to the same suspect. Once a medium has correctly guessed the suspect, location and weapon, they move their token to the epilogue board and receive one clairvoyancy point for each hour remaining on the clock. They can still use their remaining clairvoyancy tokens to score additional points.

If one or more mediums fail to identify their proper suspect, location and weapon before the end of the seventh hour, then the ghost has failed and dissipates, leaving the mystery unsolved. If, however, they have all succeeded, then the ghost has recovered enough of its memory to identify the culprit.

Mediums then group their suspect, location and weapon cards on the table and place a number by each group. The ghost then selects one group, places the matching culprit number face down on the epilogue board, picks three vision cards — one for the suspect, one for the location, and one for the weapon — then shuffles these cards. Players who have achieved few clairvoyancy points flip over one vision card at random, then secretly vote on which suspect they think is guilty; players with more points then flip over a second vision card and vote; then those with the most points see the final card and vote.

If a majority of the mediums have identified the proper suspect, with ties being broken by the vote of the most clairvoyant medium, then the killer has been identified and the ghost can now rest peacefully. If not, well, perhaps you can try again...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
I'm surprised at how much I enjoy this one but I've been charmed by it so far. We play where the psychic is not allowed to show his/her card to the other players but rather must interpret it verbally to them. If they fail the first guess, then they may reveal their card for more help; works really well.

I like the bidding mechanism only because it gives the psychic players something else to do on their turn and keeps them even more engaged with other players' guesses.

After some rough first games, we've been winning lately so I wonder if it's getting too easy for us and we need to go from medium to hard mode. I'm also feeling like I'm ready for more dream cards. 

Dixit feels like more of a game and this is more of a group activity, but I still enjoy it. Only time will tell if the charm still holds up or if there isn't enough game to hold my interest.

RATING: 8.75
I love, love, love:
- the artwork
- the cooperative nature of interpreting each others' wild and vivid dreams
- the eruption of discussion that happens at the end of every game
- the agony of trying to understand a very confused ghost
- the agony of being the very confused ghost

I dislike:
- the timer, so we don't play with it
- that the game's finale seems sorta lacking in impact

Final verdict: It's Clue but prettier and funner! The only big drawback is that the finale is not as gripping as the rest of the game. With our usual two-psychic game on Easy, Medium, or Hard difficulty, you're often using one dream card to decide between 4-6 possibilities each (suspects, locations, and items); at the end of the game, though, you're using 1-3 cards to decide between just two options, and this is true regardless of the number of players--that the finale gives you much better chances at guessing correctly.

RATING: 10
BUY MYSTERIUM.

Played Mysterium 12+ times.

My favorite big group game.

Why?
1. Everyone is on a team and gets to help each other out.
2. Non-board gamers love it. You don't have to be strategic to do well. You don't have to be smart. You don't have to be a quick thinker. It's perfect for everyone.
3. Since it's entirely co-op there is no fighting. (Which happens in the regular Dixit game, sadly)
4. Beautiful artwork that everyone gets to study and ponder.

After my first game night with it, I went to my game store and bought Dixit cards to match with it. Not all Dixit will work well with the game. I looked at all of them and bought Dixit: Memories and Dixit: Quest. This added 168 new "vision" cards and were only $20 each. This was a better solution for me than getting the actual expansion, Hidden Signs, which only comes with 42 vision cards. HOWEVER, I WILL be buying the expansion as well because I want the 12 new character, location, and object cards. I hear it makes the game harder (which is what I want). I love having a difficult time knowing who you are... "Am I the cop, the hunter, or the war general!!!? I don't know. They all have guns and I got a sheep holding a gun!" That's the best.

If you're hyper competitive, an alpha gamer, and a huge Euro game fan, this one is not for you. People still make silly deductions. People can be stubborn, "But Grandpa, you're definitely this location." Grandpa puts his vote on another location. Nope. "Grandpa, look, you see that in the picture? I think that's pointing to this location." Grandpa still puts it on another location. Nope. Then he finally puts it on the one you suggested. Yep. 

But hey, whatcha gonna do? It's his turn. He can lose us the game if he wants to (which he did) BUT guess what, I just made a quick managerial decision and added another 2 turns to the game. They were happy. I was happy. Make the game fun for your friends.

Best way to play the game is with the Ghost not speaking. Knock twice for yes, once for no, or vice versa. 

Set up takes a while, but it can be expedited if you delegate.
- Have one person pick out the # of character cards they want then match those cards with the Ghosts cards (And do this for the locations and weapons)
- You set up the other contents while they get the cards.

I cut out some cardboard pieces and added some buttons, expanding the game to be played by 11 people total (including ghost). 

Another huge thing that I do differently than the rules suggest, is that I give ONLY 1 card to each player each round. My understanding from the rule book is that you can give as many cards as you want to a person in a single round. This would be far too easy. But hey, if the game is too hard, make the necessary changes for you to enjoy it.

Buy this game. Then buy Dixit: Memories and Dixit: Quest. Then buy Mysterium: Hidden Signs.

RATING: 5
Elkerülhetetlen a Dixittel való összehasonlítás; míg a Dixitben szabadon szárnyalhat a fantázia, itt 7 kézben tartott kártya keretei közé van szorítva. Eddigi tapasztalat, hogy mindenki szellem szeretne lenni. Én nem. Túlságosan nehéz kiválasztani a kiosztandó kártyákat, esetemben AP veszélyes a dolog. És nagyon véletlenszerű, semmint végig gondolt tudatos döntés.
A játék mindenesetre szemet gyönyörködtető! Kapunk „anyagot” a pénzünkért. Jelölők, kártyák, kellékek, tokenek mind-mind az élvezeti faktort hivatottak növelni, sikerrel. Az elődjéhez képesti újítások ötletesek, mint pl a homokóra, ami hasznos a játékidő kordában tartásában. De a legérdekesebb újítás a látnoki képességsáv- és jelölők, amivel megtippelhetjük, hogy a többi médium helyesen szavazott-e a saját kártyájára, és ennek függvényében szavazunk majd a legvégén a végső közös látomásban. Tehát mindenképpen szebb és jobb, mint a Tajemnicze Domostwo, de…
De mégsem élvezetes annyira, amennyire lehetne! Ez egy partijáték, de túl időigényes az előkészület. A játékszabály részletes, talán túlságosan is szájbarágós.
igazán akartam szeretni ezt a játékot, de csak feltételesen sikerült. Érzem az igyekezetet a készítők részéről, hogy próbálták hangulatilag maximalizálni, de kissé erőltetettnek érzem az eredményt. Túl sok negatív dolog jött ki belőlem, pedig annyira azért nem rossz játék, csak nálam valahogy a negatív oldala domborodott ki a hangulata helyett, sajnos. Biztosan elő fog még kerülni, de félő nem olyan gyakran, mint kellene.

RATING: 9
BEAUTIFUL GAME, high quality cards, and striking art. This game can be either hilarious, or suspensful depending on the group (and beverages consumed) One player is a ghost and tries to convey the killer,location, and weapon to the other players, who are psychics. This is done by the ghost giving cards with striking art to each psychic, Each card has many things going on in foreground and background. The ghost tries to send a clue through this card, which represents an abstract dream/vision the psychic recieved. Each player has to guess a specific SET of the three. At the end, only one interpretation is correct, and all  players must vote. A lot of fun, deep thinking without complxity.

RATING: 6
Mysterium is a great-looking game, all the way from the box to each of the components. The full-frame large-format character and location cards are pretty much unparalleled, greatly contributing to the mysterious-yet-approachable feel of the game. However, in my experience, the gameplay itself fails to consistently deliver an enjoyable experience for different types of players: interpreting the twisted visions in the cards can range from delightful, to just meh, or all the way to boring or frustrating. So as much as the atmosphere can be captivating, the enjoyment provided by the core mechanic falls quite short, at least for me, in comparison to the great fun you could have with other party/family guessing games like Codenames.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Ok, first up, right-brain, arbitrary party style games aren't really my thing, but I have to admit they do have their place in any balanced games collection.  
It's actually quite fun to play a game occasionally that isn't analytical, especially one so well produced as this one, which alone constitutes 10/10.

My wife was really taken with this one; hardly surprising since she loves Dixit.  

If I was scoring this purely on the BGG scale and my desire to play in preference to my preferred Euros, I would probably score it a 6.   However, as a party style game I would give it a 8 to 9.  My rating is a reflection of all of these elements.

If there is one element in the game that fails slightly then it's the end game.  After all the rounds guessing suspects, the final "whodunit" comes down to 1 guess where the majority wins or loses.  I'm not sure how this could have been done better but it was slightly anti-climatic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Purchased this based on the hype and it has mostly lived up to that. I really like it personally, but I could see it falling flat with some groups or getting old after awhile. My family is split on this - we have people who love it and people who have a hard time with the abstract thinking.  I think we may be house-ruling this one - for example, we may not use the timer, or may apply it also to the ghost, or we may not use the "vote" tokens, or if we do, we may not use the individual standings to view the final clues, and we definitely do voting on the final test in a different way, by identifying which clue alligns with which category. There's a lot of business going on that seems to get in the way of just having a fun romp with this game.  Like set-up and clean up are putzy, and there's a lot of down time as the ghost is thinking. Also, we pretty much let the ghost talk as long as s/he refrains from commenting on the game.

Some people say Mysterium should replace Dixit, but I don't see it this way. They share one game mechanism (guessing someone's "meaning" in an obscure picture) and beyond that the objectives are pretty different.

RATING: 7
Cluedo meets Dixit - Mr Green in the Parlour with the Rope but this time you must deduce the murderer by discerning the truth from the often very vague and tenuous clues given in the form of a very beautiful but not necessarily very relevant picture on a Dixit card which represents the ghost of the victim trying to get in touch with you in your dreams to reveal the culprit.The ghost player has the most involvement in the game while the players playing the psychics mostly just tag along for the ride. RATING: 8
Great theme. Mechanics fit the theme well. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Each hour (i.e., game turn), the ghost hands one or more vision cards face up to each medium, refilling their hand to seven each time they share vision cards. These vision cards present dreamlike images to the mediums, with each medium first needing to deduce which suspect corresponds to the vision cards received. Once the ghost has handed cards to the final medium, they start a two-minute sandtimer. Once a medium has placed their token on a suspect, they may also place clairvoyancy tokens on the guesses made by other mediums to show whether they agree or disagree with those guesses.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The designer obviously played "Dixit" and thought it would be cool to combine it with "Clue" and make it cooperative. An important change from "Dixit", though, is that the "active player" never changes. One player is the ghost and must help the other players solve various murders by giving them cards with visual clues for location, weapon and perpetrator of each crime.

The problem is that, when all players solve their assigned crimes, they must find out which of those is the murder of the ghost character. According to how successful their previous guesses were, each player sees one to three cards and must secretly choose which crime refers to the ghost. Victory or defeat is determined by this single voting, and the rest of the game just serves to set how many cards each player can see. It still is an interesting and enjoyable game, but losing because a majority of players made a wrong guess at this crucial moment can be very frustrating.

RATING: 8.8
Mysterium is a game that delivers bags of ambiance when played under the right conditions; in our session, we had the lights down low, the Mysterium soundtrack playing, and a strict 'the ghost makes no sound' (aside from knocks for yes/no) policy, which added a chilling role play dimension to the proceedings.

For me, the standout aspect of Mysterium is the artwork. It's both gorgeous and bizarre, which furthers the dark atmosphere, and truly makes the game come alive (...excuse the pun). The mechanics - 'Dixit meets Cluedo' - are solid, but it is the marriage with the theme that elevates the experience.

Playing as a psychic had practically no learning curve. Simply discuss hypothesis with fellow psychics - and then make a simple choice. I felt valuable and involved from the very first play-through with other experienced players, with my interpretations of certain cards adding an additional consideration.

Playing as the ghost requires a little more understanding, and a few things to keep track of, but nothing too taxing. 

The potential flaw with Mysterium, is after a few play throughs, players may know to correspond certain dream cards with specific people, places and locations. This is a double-edged sword however. In a recent game, the ghost provided a dream card that the psychics automatically assumed meant the policeman - due to it being used as such on previous play-throughs - only for it to actually have represented someone else.

Overall, this is a very good game, elevated to a great game if you are willing to invest in the theme and get lost in the ambiance.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I was worried that this game would require the perfect lighting or setting, or  mood to full enjoy this game, such as it's only good on Halloween, or I need to set up a seance to make Mysterium great. I was glad that I was wrong...and boy how glad I was. The guys at Dicetower, whom I pretty much see to eye-to-eye on their opinions, were completely wrong on this one. After 5 plays I can whole-heartedly say Mysterium is just a great game in any situation.

It plays fairly quick, has great components, easy to teach and, to me, is a great gateway and is up there with some of the other great gateway games like Ticket to Ride, Shadows Over Camelot,7 Wonders etc. 

My two small quibbles is that having a ghost player that is having some difficulty with being able to think outside the box or help with giving out clues can become kind of detrimental. And the new rules I honestly don't care too much for. I feel it can break the spirit(no pun intended) of the game by adding unnecessary "competitive" aspects. It's a full co-op game. I use the original, Tajemnicze Domostwo's polish rules, and the game is still awesome. I may try the new rules one day, but not in a rush to do so.
One of my favorites of 2015.

The game has fallen a bit for me, people have to really be in the mood to play it. If you look at it, it's not technically a game but more a social interaction amongst players. If you have one person that's just lame and doesn't want to play, the game will fall apart fast, hence why I am very careful in who I pick to play this game with now

RATING: 10
This is an amazing game.  It was our fourth game of the day, we didn't start playing it until about 23:00 and we ended up playing it four times in succession, the only game of the day to get a reply.  Part of that, of course, is because it's relatively short; it takes about 42 minutes to play...it's brilliant though, very different from our usual kind of game.  Think cluedo, but (initially) you're all trying to put together a different combination of murderer/location/weapon, and you're doing it based on 'visions' given to you by a silent ghost; these 'visions' are pictures that the ghost has to try to relate to the murderer/location/weapon (and you have to guess what the link is).  Loads of fun!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I really wanted to like this more than I do. I love Dixit and the conceit for how this game uses similar ideas to solve a mystery is compelling. In actual play, after three sessions with two groups, the fun just wasn't clicking for anyone. The biggest potential issue is that for the entire hour of play one person is giving out all of the clues. There is definitely an art to reading the group in games like Codenames, Dixit, Apples to Apples, etc. In those games, the judge role turns over fast enough that everyone gets a shot and oddball tastes are a spice, not the main course. In Mysterium, there was palpable frustration for both players and ghost as failures to communicate compound over rounds with a fail state. It's too long from when the ghost starts clue-giving to when they can talk out their logic and commiserate with the others. I very much admire Mysterium, especially the art, but I can't imagine playing it again over Codenames or another party game with shorter cycles.

RATING: 8
This game was a nice surprise to me. The argument of the game is that you are in a haunted mansion where the ghost is a former employee that was killed 30 years ago. On Halloween, a number of psychics go to the house and try to connect with the ghost, which is played by one player, the issue is that it happens some time ago and the memory of the ghost is fragile and he doesn't really remember and, instead of providing clear information, it communicates with the players through abstract images that relate, someway somehow, to the killer, the room and the weapon that killed him. Basically all the players have to work together in order to succeed, the ghost is on the same side, but he or she is not allow to talk throughout the game. The game should take less than an hour, so it is not a huge problem to be quiet for that time, it allows to create some nice atmosphere.
This game, to me, is closely related to Dixit: the ghost tries to tell a story through weird pictures that have to be understood by the players, and they, after, have to decide what the heck is the ghost trying to say. It takes that original mechanic of Dixit and it goes one step further. Highly recomendable for groups of different types of players.
Positive:
1. The theme is very well integrated with the mechanics
2. It is very easy to explain and to play
3. It is a different type of cooperative game as one player cannot speak or communicate
4. The cards are very beautiful and creative
5. I have not tried, but I thing that the cards of Dixit can be used as vision cards
Negative:
1. You have to be very careful about not telling, after the game, what were you trying to indicate with this or that card, because the game may lose the replayability (does that word exist? do you understand what I want to say?)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is an interesting game which crosses over to party game.    It's a co-op in which each player is an investigator trying to solve a murder or the ghost trying to give them clues.  The ghost gets a hand of cards with weird surrealistic scenes, representing dreams and visions the ghost can send.  Each investigator gets a suspect, location, and murder weapon card.  The ghost then hints to the investigators which of them has the appropriate suspect, location, or weapon card by playing image cards that relate to the investigator (rather than directly to the murder card).  Each investigator has a colorful persona (e.g., artist) that provides a basis to relate to the cards.  It's a bit of an odd mechanic but provides a greater range of associations.  The players then try to figure out the clues.  While it is co-op, players can definitely compete to be the MVP by making the best guesses.  There is enough thinking that it works as a strategy game while it is light enough to also work as a party game.  It's not a first choice for me but I wouldn't turn down a game if my friends wanted to play,
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Mysterium is an interesting game and puts a unique spin on the "interpreting art" concept popularized in Dixit, but I find that its structure as a co-op game lessens the experience. It doesn't feel like the game warrants a table full of people discussing and interpreting clues. This becomes apparent at the game's end when everyone has to solve a puzzle independently and come to a consensus without discussion. That was easily the most enjoyable portion of the game and one I could see sustaining a longer experience.

While being the ghost is the most rewarding (and challenging) part of the game, it is a bit disappointing that only one person at the table gets to tackle this position while everyone else plays a much lesser role.

The game has great art and some good ideas, but I wish the game imposed a bit more structure on how players communicate - I believe that would be a much more interesting challenge.

RATING: 8
2015-11-24

Initial Rating: 8.0 (November 2015)

I love Mysterium. I have the previous edition (Tajemnicze Domostwo) and I also own the new Asmodee edition. I still haven’t read the rules so I don’t know if there is reason to keep both games in my game collection. I wanted to see what are the rules´ differences but when we played Mysterium we were only 3 players so the gameplay was exactly as before (or so the game explainer told me). I plan to play it again soon to see for myself. I know that players now have some tokens but I don’t know how to use them.

On the other hand I really appreciate the change components wise. In particular I really like that the ghost now has a screen that helps him to keep his cards organized. Also I noted that the dream cards remain the same but the suspect, place and object cards feature new art. I liked it but I also liked the old art. I’m undecided which one is the best one.

Mysterium takes Dixit´s core mechanism and turns it into a great cooperative game with simple rules. The art is GREAT. Love the theme. I think it is best as a 4 player game, with more the game begins to drag with lots of downtime. I feel the ghost player has the most fun, but the game is very fun overall. 

So far I don’t have any complaint about the game, It is hard to beat but I like that. Perhaps the game comes with very few cards (has a low replay value), so if you play often some patterns will emerge (same clues for same suspect/place/object) but that can be easily solved using Dixit cards.

Bottom line, I’m rating Mysterium the same I rated Tajemnicze Domostwo as the gameplay remains the same (for 3 players at least). So far I have only seen improvement in the components´ department but I’m very keen in playing the game again soon. I will read the rules to see what changed between editions and when I do I will come back to comment again.

Current Rating: 8.0
[hr]
2016-01-27

I still haven’t played more of this edition, however I have played lots of the previous edition and I just downgraded its rating because my desire to play it has decreased a bit. So I’m also decreasing the rating of the newer edition. 

Current Rating: 7.5

2016-06-14

At last I played Mysterium with enough players to feel the difference. After all players have correctly guessed their suspects, places and objects, now each player has to guess one more and if the majority of players guessed right, all players win. I really like it! I feel it is a minor improvement over the previous version of the game. I particularly like that each player gets to see 1,2 or 3 cards depending upon their performance in the previous phases.

All things considered, I think the Asmodee edition is better than the others, but I’m still unsure if I will keep both them or not. Perhaps the expansion can help me decide, or perhaps I will keep both editions.

Current Rating: 7.5

RATING: 8
As a fan of Dixit, I love playing this game. Its cooperative mechanism is more interesting than other games I've played, because it only involves players' choices. There is a lot of conversation around the table, and playing the ghost is really fun. Although it has been compared to Cluedo (you have to find the assassin, the place and the weapon of the crime), only the theme is shared with it: the mechanisms are far from being random and there are no dice-rolls involved! A great game for imaginative people, who like to play with their friends and family. Better with more than 4 players.

詭祕莊園 是個合作遊戲，遊戲中考驗玩家間彼此的默契及心靈相通的程度，新版配件增加了鬼魂檔板，讓扮演鬼魂的玩家可以更專注於挑選卡片以及尋找相似的提示元素，而在後期揭露元兇有著更挑戰性的任務，每個靈媒玩家除了找出自己的線索之外，還需要協助並參與其他靈媒的判斷，以提升"靈視等級"，增加後續追查真兇的正確率，所以玩家間是無法 silence disengagement (自掃門前雪)，這樣的機制讓遊戲性大為提升，也讓玩家彼此的連結趨於相近，我覺得是這款遊戲相當成功的地方。

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
All I knew before playing Mysterium is the Clue heritage of it combined with Dixit cards. What sounded intriguing, turned out to be a group-dependent communication exercise that failed to grab me notwithstanding that the majority of the group knew the game before and enjoys it enough to repeatedly play it.

The main offender for me is the scoring system which is essential for seeing more clues at game end to find the final solution. To score points, players have to gauge the correctness of other players guesses on their character, location and murder weapon. Mostly, it's about knowing what the game master aims at with his hints. Once this recognition process has fallen into known conventions, the decision about the correctness of guesses loses all interest with all players then making the same guesses.

The artwork and theme are enticing, the game fails in the mechanisms.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Dixit basic mechanic with a further purpose which makes it more engaging.

RATING: 8
Mysterium is a blast. Who wouldn't want to play a psychic attempting to solve the murder of an incorporeal being? It's a wonderfully refreshing twist on the formula of Clue, the classic in which its roots reside. The nonverbal aspect of the ghost is an awesome gameplay mechanic, but it is also what creates the most frustrating part of the game. If you don't know the person who is the ghost, then interpreting the cards they give you as a psychic can be difficult at times. All in all, a wonderful game!

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I review this while noting that I haven't actually learned how to play as the ghost (it's a to-do for the future). 

First of all, this game is all about the artwork, and the artwork is effing fantastic, absolutely worth expletives of awe. For this reason, and its passing similarity to Clue, this game has gotten to the table way more often than I expected - it's still a bit specific to people who are predisposed to humor me with "just one game", but it has been quite successful every time we've played. 

The setup is pretty intense, and we haven't played enough to really streamline it. Because there are so many pieces and several different play aspects, new players really chomp at the bit to learn about all the pieces and ideas, even though really, it just needs some patience while the ghost does their thing. In the future, I think we'll try to open this up while also having a short filler game ready for non-ghost players to keep them occupied. (Love Letter is a strong contender here, especially since they are thematically kind of similar enough). 

I would say the one big drawback, and the reason this doesn't hit 9 or 10 on the ratings, is the rulebook, which is really confusing and poorly organized. I'm very glad we learned via family who already knew the game, because I think learning it from scratch would have been pretty difficult and frustrating. It's still kind of annoying to have to go back and answer questions using the rulebook, since it's often not clear where one would go to answer the questions. The game also tries to be coy by naming all the pieces thematic things like "clairvoyancy tokens", but that doesn't end up being helpful since it's not obvious which of the pieces is actually the clairvoyancy token. 

I also worry a little that play value will be decreased slightly over time as players get used to a certain ghost's playstyle and thought process, but at that point, expansions will be considered and new ghosts trained up, because the game itself is really good and I am never unhappy to get a chance with that artwork.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Definitely dependent upon having a good player playing the ghost.  Easy to confuse a couple rules as well.  It can really be difficult to find a good card for a clue as the ghost.  It seems like more of a game than Dixit as your ultimately working to find your person, place, and thing.  It's also neat that each player has their own combination to find and then at the end having to choose the real culprit from among all of them.  The art is beautiful, of course, and overall nicer than Dixit (I believe though perhaps purposefully more detailed).  The screen works better than any game I've ever seen (And I've seen a lot!) with how you put things into the pockets and such.  After a few games even our 8 year old son was able to play the ghost reasonably well.  We most often play with 3 and its great with that number.  2 player wasn't bad by any stretch either.  We've not played with enough players yet to use the other tokens that make the game competitive, but enjoy playing it purely cooperatively instead.  We've gone ahead and picked up the expansion which adds loads more of each type of card.  Wonderful physical components and card quality as well all around.

RATING: 8

It's very similar to Dixit in a way.

We played it with Dixit cards and it also worked pretty well.

If it would have more cards included I would maybe give it a 8.5 or 9. But maybe with the upcoming expansion and more cards I will increase the rating.

Suggestion: use Dixit cards for 7 players to have more clues :-)

RATING: 7

This will be a great addition to the Betrayal at House on the Hill & Arkham Horror for Halloween time. RATING: N/A
Unable to talk, the amnesic ghost communicates with the mediums through visions, which are represented in the game by illustrated cards. The mediums must decipher the images to help the ghost remember how he was murdered: Who did the crime? Where did it take place? Which weapon caused the death? The more the mediums cooperate and guess well, the easier it is to catch the right culprit.

In Mysterium, a reworking of the game system present in Tajemnicze Domostwo, one player takes the role of ghost while everyone else represents a medium. To solve the crime, the ghost must first recall (with the aid of the mediums) all of the suspects present on the night of the murder. A number of suspect, location and murder weapon cards are placed on the table, and the ghost randomly assigns one of each of these in secret to a medium.

RATING: 7
Dixit meets Clue. One player is a traumatized spirit. The other players are mediums trying to interprete the spirit's dreamlike visions. The objective of the game is for all mediums to guess who killed the spirit, where he was killed and with what object.

This game is somewhat overproduced and has a lot of components. Don't get me wrong, the game looks fantastic. But setting up the game can be quite a lengthy process, especially considering what the game boils down to.

I like the game slightly more than Dixit, but Dixit plays faster and all players are doing the same. Getting to play the spirit can be a lot of fun, but it can also be frustrating ordeal. I do like that it can play up to 7 players. A game I will play when I'm in the mood for it.

RATING: 5
Despite the gorgeous artwork and the cool premise I don't really understand the huge hype for this game. It's basically charades with pictures after all, and while charades isn't a bad game and there's a little bit of hand management in this game I don't think it should be highly lauded. Also, 42ish minutes is a long time to only achieve getting 4 correct guesses. In addition, I dislike how the only collaboration is discussion, as any "aid" you could give to others could actually make them choose the wrong card.

Compared to Dixit the combination of no word clues and also that it's a co-op helps prevents giving super specific clues that only one person can get, so guess per guess I think it's better implemented with only a slight I missing of the aspect of Dixit of wanting to be netiher too obscure or obvious. However, as previously stated in Mysterium you simply don't get to have as many guesses per game.

EDIT: The tokens you can use to endorse or refute another person's choice adds a little bit of interaction, but still not enough in my opinion.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
First play fell a little flat. Too abstract for my friends; they didn't feel much tension or get into it, but the overall experience was still positive. Some good moments were had when murder weapon clues were misinterpreted (by far the most difficult stage), but plenty of others felt like the players were pretending to care to keep the game moving (or maybe I was pretending to enjoy being the ghost, because I rarely had any trouble giving clues).

I think limiting the number of dreams to one per player is an extremely important house rule. It gives each dream more weight, eliminates the possibility of the ghost doing a hand dump, and makes it easier to play cooperatively as there are fewer clues for everyone to look at.

Clairvoyance tokens are difficult to explain and feel contrived. Actually my issue is the whole game feels kind of contrived, in the sense that it puts too much window dressing and "stuff" on a simple concept, trying to force the fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
([url=http://store.401games.ca/]401games.ca[/url], 2015-10-26)

Libellud took a long time to update Mysterium and bring it to market and did so with mixed results. The cover box is outstanging, the ghost game screen is a nice addition, the new art on back of dream cars is great as well, and the clock and crow markers are nice too. On the other hand, the new art for the psychic cards is quite different, more comic book-ish and in a sense less detailed. The worst part of this version is the clairvoyance track and markers. I'm not sure why this was added to the game, maybe to ensure that all players paid attention to everyone's dream cards which in a cooperative game shouldn't a problem in the first place, but it adds fiddlyness to the game which makes it less elegant than the original. The silent shared vision is also less interesting for a cooperative game. The best version of the rules remains the initial version.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.7
(review after only two play as "ghost")
Great presentation; the components, art, and "fluff" is all top notch.  Easy to get in character as the ghost.  Game is harder than it seems at first, which is a good thing.  I look forward to playing it again, although my group responded to the first play of the game with some mixed feelings; some were eager to play it again right away while others were somewhat frustrated by the difficulty and what they perceived as opacity.  

Playing it again I noticed that it was much smoother, and everyone in the group enjoyed it, players of different ages, experience, and style.  It is definitely a crowd pleaser and unique among games (especially if someone has never played Dixit).  I have some concerns with replayability, but definitely a solid addition to any collection.

RATING: 6
Interesting game which is like a super frustrating but more unique take on Clue. The ghost player really needs to be on their game with the visions they give the psychics, otherwise everyone is in for a rough time. Of course, there's only so much you can do as the ghost, which is where the frustration comes in. I think a lot of ghost players will probably err on the side of "lots of clues" - a double-edged sword which I'm not sure is always the best choice unless the recurring theme in the chosen set of clues is incredibly obvious.

Not sure if I like the "killer is chosen at the very end" mechanic. Thematically it doesn't make any sense, since if the ghost knows whodunnit, why would they bother giving all but one of the psychics incorrect visions? Of course, if that were the case then it could only really work as a 2-player game so whatever. It's still fun.

RATING: 9.2
This is like Dixit, but cooperative and much better. If you're not sure what Dixit is, it's like Balderdash with art instead of words, and much better.

In Mysterium, one player plays as a ghost who has enlisted a team of psyhics (all the other players), in hopes that they will help him solve his murder and get closure. The ghost communicates to all the other players solely by sending them visions (i.e. cards with very obscure art), and the players use this to determine possible suspects, murder locations, and weapons in order to solve the case.

RATING: 8
+ Hidden Signs expansion (includes promo cards P1-3)

Rating based on 2, 3, 6 and 7 players.

A cross between Dixit and Codenames, but I prefer picture clues over words and the longer narrative over having lots of multiple rounds, and the co-operative gameplay makes the game lively with plenty of tabletalk. I have played both with and without the clairvoyancy track, but for my own tastes I think it improves the game by creating a bit more group suspense, and would help alleviate potential alpha gamer problems (don't agree with someone? Just put your token down and leave it at that). Playing without it is still fine though, and is probably the way to go if playing with non-gamers. 

There's a fair amount of setup time needed, and since the ghost isn't supposed to talk to the other players it's definitely not at its best with 2.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Mysterium is a murder mystery game with a creative twist.  It's a co-operative game in which one player takes on the role of a ghost, and the other players are psychics trying to help the ghost solve his murder of about 100 years before.

This is done through the distribution of Dixit-like cards by the ghost player to the psychic players.  The cards represent "visions" that the psychics have.  They then interpret these visions, and use the clues within them to narrow down suspects, locations, and weapons a la Clue.

This is the only means of communication the ghost has with the psychics.  The psychics, on the other hand, can speak with each other to give each other aid.  They'll need it too, because there's only 7 turns for the proper suspects, locations, and weapons to get picked.  From them the actual murderer must be discovered.  If this doesn't happen the group loses and the ghost continues to be tied to this plane of reality.

Mysterium is a fantastic game!  The artwork is top notch, the theme is intriguing, and the gameplay is really fun.  I had high hopes for this one, and it met them all.  Couldn't recommend this more highly. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4
This sounds like a great game on paper, with the same Social, Story-Telling and Guessing mechanics as Dixit, along a nod to the clue-gathering mystery solving mechanics of Clue Do.  

In practice, the game is great for the Investigator players, but is a little burdensome for the Ghost. I feel it's a little overrated because it fails to really fix the roles so the ghost can enjoy the game instead of just stressing out keeping the structure of the game all while trying to provide the correct clues. 

If you have one player in your group who loves being the Ghost, though, then this game would be a near perfect score. Otherwise, I find that it puts too much burden on the Ghost role to recommend. 

Worse, if you have Deception, well all I can say is Deception/CS Files is just better than this game in every way while scratching mostly the same itch. 

I don't get why this game is so popular but I feel that gamers should give this a pass in favor of better games like Dixit or Deception.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Overview:
Mysterium is a cooperative game where the players work together to solve a murder mystery and set free the ghost of the murder victim within 7 rounds. It involves unspoken player interaction, and can be surprisingly deep while still appealing to families with gamers of all ages.

Summary:
A beautifully designed interactive playing experience with tight gameplay mechanics that is fun for the whole family! I bring it to all of my friends board game nights, and even to family events, and everyone loves playing it.

Art?
Great! From abstract art, to depicting potential murderers, and overall atmosphere, the art is high quality, fits the game, and enhances the experience. 

Quality?
The cards and other materials are all of high quality. Cards get touched and passed around a lot and hold up well.

Theme?
The theme is not particularly profound, but is fun. You can play a whole game without thinking about the thematic goal, but the art helps to bring it to your mind occasionally, and a heavy theme was honestly just not needed. 

One almost weakness (more like a missed opportunity maybe?) is that the game developed out story for each "psychic", and you choose color corresponding to one psychic when you begin the game, but the psychic you pick does not really matter. Personally, I would love to see an expansion where the psychics are given minor unique gameplay abilities, but it would likely be tough to fit into the already tight gameplay. Just a way I think the theme could influence the gameplay more.

Gameplay?
The gameplay of this game is simple, yet fantastic. One player plays the ghost - the murder victim. They pass cards of very abstract art to the other players - who play psychics. The ghost tries to use those cards to indicate to the players who the murderer, murder location, and murder weapon might be. Players playing psychics work together to interpret the card art because the ghost cannot speak. Its an interactive experience that can incorporate shy players and outgoing players. 

Playing the ghost vs psyshcics is a very different experience, which adds a lot of variety to the gameplay. The ghost is a stressful experience - in a good way - because you only get 7 cards to choose from. You do not always have the "perfect" abstract art card, so you sometimes have to use multiple cards over multiple rounds and hope the players pick up on patterns. As they say, "its all up to interpretation" and that makes the game a lot of fun.

One weakness is that the success of a good chunk game lies in the ghost's hands. If you have someone who "overthinks" or tries to be too literal, the psychics will likely have a very tough time guessing the right cards, and that can be frustrating. I had that happen one time. It's a rare occurrence though I think. 

Other issues are a lot of potential down time, depending on how long the ghost takes to issue cards. This if often due to a strange timing mechanic meant to pressure psychics into interpreting clues quickly, but that has no actually stress since the ghost can take as long as they like giving out clues before the timer starts. We just stopped using the timer to be honest.

Replayability?
A lot! Switching between roles adds a lot of diversity, and the combination of cards in the ghosts hand can change up how any single murder, location, or weapon needs to be communicated. I have played it many times, and my family of "traditional gamers" (i.e. "the farther we will go is Catan") is very willing to play this game when I suggest it - and they even bring it up on their own sometimes! *cue the angel choir*

One replay issue is that once a card pops up in several games, you begin to have an "insider" understanding of what clues the card is good for, so adding new players to the game - especially as the ghost - is likely essential for long-term replayability.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 3
