RATING: 7
[b]Like:[/b]
-Funny
-Theme, that's also similar to the well known game Clue

[b]Dislike:[/b]
-Long set-up
-The amount of components might scare new gamers away
-The need to explain rules while you're the ghost makes the game lose it's immersion

I want to play this a little more (and with more people), but it was pretty funny so far. Set-up takes a while though, which I did not expect when buying this game.

This is kinda a problem for what's supposed to be a gateway game. "Hey guys, wanna play a game? Don't worry it's really easy..." *proceeds to grab dozens of components and shuffle multiple decks*. This is also why it's been so hard to get to the table.

Also, you aren't supposed to speak as the ghost, which is kinda hard when you also need to explain the rules. And letting someone else be the ghost is not really gateway level easy anymore.

However, it is the only cooperative board game I know of that's easy to teach and not prone to quarterbacking (unlike Pandemic, so I have heard).

RATING: 6
Based on my plays of the app. The game is fine. I found it fun for the first couple of plays. There are good and bad things about being the investigators or the ghosts, but ultimately it suffers from what I like to call the Pictionary Effect. Basically, if you do a bad job at giving or deciphering clues, the other person will blame you for it. A lot of times the ghost just doesn't have any good cards to play though, which helps to facilitate this negative reaction. I will say that I enjoyed this more than Deception: Murder in Hong Kong, though it has far less replay value in comparison. Deception has tons and tons of different cards, whereas in Mysterium you'll see most of what it offers by the 3rd or 4th game. The difference, however, is that I like having to make connections between the clues and the guilty cards in this game a lot more since they usually have little to nothing in common with each other. This is something I believe is done better here than in games like Dixit. I think the game is alright for what it is, but it isn't something I'd want to play all that often.

RATING: 7
What makes this game is the art. It's pretty straightforward: there are only so many dead people, rooms, and weapons, so if you don't solve each clue in order right away, process of elimination works. The art tho. Every card is complex, often with stories tucked away in juxtapositions you don't even notice until the second or third play. To unlock the joy of this game, you really need a good ghost: If the person playing ghost can make the best use of limited, very dream-weird and beautiful cards (think Dixit) given the skills and tendencies of the other players, it's going to be fascinating. What limits this game is that you can't really get into your 'part' (unless you really dig race caricature). It would be so much more fun to argue over why your clue matches your answer if you could pretend, guilt-free, to have a divination method (clairvoyance, crystals, cards, whatever) you can describe mysteriously to other players. Discussing whether the ghost meant you to notice matching hues on your clue card and in the card one of the people/places/weapons from which you're supposed to choose, or whether the mist-shrouded orchard on your clue card means hedge clippers were the murder weapon or that the weapon was made of wood, is fun - but it would be more fun if the player piece you'd been assigned wasn't a magic-jewel-ring-wearing Arab or an I-Ching reading Chinese woman or one of the other equally squicky options. Meh. Make up different characteristics and backstories, put a heavily top-shaded bright lamp on the table (and give the ghost an LED reading light) and turn off all the other lights, cue up some storm sounds or unsettling music (try Charles Ives!), and let the art bemuse and absorb you while the ghost struggles (with a fairly small hand) to send the clearest dream-imagery to help you find your solution. Definitely better among imaginative types and with at least 3 players.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Mysterium is what you get when you mash together Clue and Dixit, tying the games together with a theme of a ghost trying to identify it's murderer to the members of a séance. It sounds like an interesting concept, but the execution is terrible!

First of all, why is everyone trying to identify different people, places, and weapons? How many times was this ghost murdered? Oh, only the final clues indicate the killer? Then what was the point of identifying a bunch of not-murderers?

Secondly, using dreamy Dixit imagery is a nonsensical way to indicate the facts of the murder. Clue cards should be more grounded in reality. It would be easy to make hodgepodge images without resorting to outright fantasy and would be better thematically.

Thirdly, why does the game have to be played in stages; People, then Places, and finally Things? Why can't guesses be made out of order and clues given to players be persistent, instead of getting wiped after each correct guess?

Were all these issues addressed, the result would be a 2-player game, which would likely lower the developer's profit margin, but it would improve gameplay greatly. Mysterium's asymmetrical design with the current player count makes for long delays waiting for cards to be chosen for everyone, which puts a frustrating amount of pressure on the Ghost player.

Apparently the Clairvoyance tokens were an addition to the English release of Mysterium. Why? Was it necessary for someone to be crowned King of the Cooperators? Wasn't winning the game enough?

Oh, and the components suck, especially the Clairvoyance scoring tokens. I've never seen a smaller chunk of cardboard intended for gameplay. The dividers for the table are pointless. If it is that important that cards be placed in specific areas, yet you're not willing to provide a board, then include a roll-up mat of felt or neoprene. Finally, the box insert is an impediment. The owner of the game I played had to resort to lifting the insert out to store components underneath to get the box lid to fit.

Thankfully I didn't manage to trade for this piece of garbage in the last math trade. Bullet dodged!

RATING: 6.8
Fundamental flaw of this compared to Dixit, is it is somewhat limiting to creativity. It almost like Funemployed versus CAH. In Funemployed you impart your own creativity to the cards when telling your story, in CAH you let the cards do all the talking. Mysterium has this problem too, because the ghost can't talk it must rely totally on the ability of a random hand of cards to impart meeting. While this is a neat concept in theory, in practice it makes for a less thinky experience than Dixit.  Still that might be the mood you are in, and its certainly an awesome thematic game with great components and creepy art. But it seems to have a little less soul, or legs than Dixit.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.75
A beautiful game that captures the mood and is just right for Halloween.
The game comes with a link to the website that allows you to play background music.
In this game, players are trying to solve a very old murder.
A mystery so old, that players must receive clues from a ghost who can only be reached on Halloween night.
The ghost and players are working to cooperatively solve the murder before 7 hours are up.

The ghost player will be giving clues to the other psychic players in the form of Dixit style cards.
The psychic players will be looking at basic cards showing who could have done it, what location and what weapon was used.
As the psychics receive clue cards from the ghost, they can narrow down their choices.
The complexity in this game comes in the fact that the ghost can only send clues in the form of vague images and only with the cards he currently has available to give as clues.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
規則:
*將真相凶器地點人物進度圖版，時鐘轉到I，放置根據難度 抽出特定張數的 人物卡 地點卡 物品卡 (棕色牌背)
# Players Easy Normal Difficult 
2 4 5 6 
3 5 6 7
4 5 6 7 
5 6 7 8 9
6 6 8 9 
7 7 8 9 
簡單 每回合一隻烏鴉，普通整場三隻，困難全場一隻，插到鬼魂簿上
抽出後放置對應圖版下，然後也從鬼魂牌抽出對應數目交給鬼魂玩家，鬼魂玩家三種類型都抽出對應玩家人數放到鬼魂簿上，每個玩家的對應位置
*一個玩家當鬼魂，其他當靈媒，靈媒玩家拿取對應腳色的所有顏色配件，靈視指示物4~5位玩家拿1~4，6~7全拿，直覺指示物放到人物進度圖版上，靈視指示物放到靈視軌0
*遊戲分兩個階段
1.猜測嫌疑犯階段 最多七回合，鬼魂抽7張夢卡，給完一個人提示在補回張，一次給一個人可以給多張，所有玩家都給完後倒轉沙漏，時間到後公布結果，所有靈媒可互相討論，時間內移動靈媒指示物到你認為屬於你的卡片上，同時可以放靈視指示物到別人的預測上(X代表認為他猜錯，勾猜對)
>猜對的玩家移動指示物到下一個要猜的上面，猜錯的移回去，用掉的靈視指示物移除，放對的增加靈視軌一格
>一輪結束時間前進一格在重複進行，如果全部猜完，距離七回合有幾格就可以增加靈視軌幾格，猜到的卡卡已收到人物收納袋中
>靈視指示物使用完棄在時鐘下，在第四回合會全部收回
>七回合內只要全部都猜完就進入下個階段，否則遊戲結束
2.揭露真凶階段 靈媒將袋中的卡片都取出放成一組，靈媒挑出對應人數的鬼魂指示物用數字面放在每組上，鬼魂挑出對應數字的兇手指示物，從中選一張當作真兇，然後鬼魂從手牌妻中張給三張洗勻蓋著放，一張提示人物一張地點一張凶器
>表決階段 一張一張開，根據靈視等級，每個玩家一在不同階段將自己認為的真凶號碼(使用靈視指示物背面)放到袋中
>投票多數決，平手則是靈視等級高的結果為高，在平手比年長的贏
>指出兇手一起勝利
*****2/3人***
*每個靈媒使用兩組，揭露真相時，三張卡都開著
*兩人時要額外從沒使用的卡片中抽出兩組，總共四組來找真兇
*3人時最後要討論兩人達成共識決定誰是真兇

RATING: 7
Same comment as the original really (follows below). I like the addition of the bets on who's right and wrong, leading to a variation of the end game which is fine (but not altogether enough to warrant an upgrade from the original), but a lot of the English version is otherwise Clancy of the Overchrome with no substantial gaming (or art) difference from the original version.
Original comment: Interesting but without being fun per se, being a constant analysis of how the spirit player might be trying to link two pictures together; and when you can see multiple possible links, taking a punt at which is the most likely. After a few games you get to see the same cards again, and remembered analyses of previous cards come into play creating a meta game of link patterns. Which can only be advantageous to the players, but it seems like a creation of "cheats" which circumvents the point of play, so I'm not sure how much replay the game's going to have within a same group of players. At the least it creates a nice social experience of shared discussion and contemplation which gives it a different feel from other games in my collection so it'll probably find a permanent spot.

RATING: 9
Mysterium combines elements of Dixit and Clue into a cooperative whodunit that takes less than an hour (with proper focus). The artwork ranges from awe-inducing cuteness to some extreme trippiness. One player fills the role of the ghost of a person who was murdered, while all other players (up to 6) are psychics trying to communicate with the dead to solve the crime.
The ghost silently gives clues, in the form of cards with artwork on them to help the players identify who killed him, where it happened, and what the weapon was. The psychics must go in order of who, where, and finally what. Each of them has individual cards that they are trying to identify. In each category there are a number of cards to select from, the number of cards changes based on difficulty and number of players. Psychics get 7 rounds to determine their who, what, and where. If any psychic fails, the game is lost.
After the players have each identified the who, what, and where assigned to them, you enter the final round. Everyone’s set of cards creates the final line-up. The ghost now needs to choose three clues from her hand hand to get all of the psychics to solve the crime by having them all select the correct answer.
The game has a concept of clairvoyance. At the end of the game, clairvoyance indicates the number of cards a psychic gets to see before making a guess. There are two ways to gain clairvoyance. First, you get tokens to bet on whether you think the other psychics have made right or wrong guesses. If you’re correct you move up one on the clairvoyance track. The second way is to have extra rounds left after solving your individual who, where and what. You get one point of clairvoyance per remaining round. The amount of clairvoyance needed two or three cards changes depending on the number of players in the game.
Tips for playing:
Psychics need to voice their interpretations out loud and work together while the Ghost should be keeping track of what players latch on to from the visions. In the final round these will be key for picking cards to nudge players in the right direction.
Don’t forget that the Ghost is a player when considering how many cards should be displayed per section. Forgetting that leads to using too few cards (and too few clairvoyancy tokens) for the difficulty you’re trying for.
Also don’t forget that the Ghost can give one or more cards to each psychic. We overlooked that detail in the rules.
The ghost gets to choose which group of cards to nudge the players towards in the final round. For added difficulty, choose which group you need to nudge them towards at random!
If someone starts making fun of someone’s interpretation, or of them getting a guess wrong, shut that down right away. The fun depends on people being able to make open guesses.

In order to familiarize ourselves with the rules, we first played with two players. In two player mode, the psychic player ends up playing two psychics. Although we both had fun, Mysterium is definitely not at its strongest as a two player game.. Multiplayer mode allows you to collaborate with the rest of the psychics, in two player mode you only get to talk with yourself. You also don’t use clairvoyance in two player mode.
This is a great game for children, we played with three adults and four children aged 5 through 11. The recommended age for players is 10+ but the kids liked working together. Our youngest player got help from the older kids but still contributed meaningfully on his own. With a young group, it’s useful to play on easy mode so that process of elimination provides some additional help. We also didn’t use clairvoyance when playing with the kids to simplify the rules and we allowed them to discuss the options in the final round.
We played several times with clairvoyance. Mysterium is a lot of fun as a large group game. Psychics remain in engaged in the game because of the cooperative nature. Even if one person doesn’t need to be actively guessing, they will be interested in helping the rest of the group make their guesses.
One gotcha that we encountered: We played six games before realizing that the ghost can give one or more clue cards to each player per round. We accidentally played on extremely hard mode for many of our games. We recommend giving at most three cards to a single person to keep the raven mechanic meaningful.
After five games, we found that we wanted more variety in the cards we had to choose from. Fortunately the hidden signs expansion provided exactly that variety. Mysterium is a great group game with high replay value. It has become a go-to party game for us.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
I enjoy this a whole lot, but, having played it about a half-dozen times, I have had to adjust a few things. Critically, if you have a full house of players, then, being the Spirit/Ghost can take WAY too long as you try to figure out the right vision to pass on. This can leave the players really bored. So, I have introduced a rule to use the sand-timer with the game as a time limit on how long the Spirit/Ghost can take to put the visions together for the players. One other thing: I have never played with the +/- betting system for visions (which would influence how many clues the players can see at the end of the game). Even not using those, the players have never -- in 6 games -- been able to figure out the correct murderer/location/item.

RATING: 9
This is a great game with beautiful artwork.  I personally have always enjoyed playing it when I've been able to get it to the table.  The biggest drawback I've found is getting people that are willing to play.  I know my wife and friends that I normally game with have all given it a try and have been reluctant to jump back in.  For them, the abstract nature of the clues and trying to piece it together didn't do much for them.  If you've got willing people, I would definitely give this a try.

One side note, when I have played we didn't use the clairvoyance track and played it purely co-op similar to the original game.  It just worked better this way with my group and keeping them playing, so I can't comment on how well that addition works with the game.

RATING: 9
Deduction game with a very strong theme. Simply dimming the lights adds a lot to the dark, ominous atmosphere. Fully cooperative but the ghost player is not allowed to speak or give non-verbal gestures. Plays up to seven and I do not think playing with the max number would hurt the pacing too much. Would take longer but probably wouldn't feel too long. A fairly deep game that isn't heavy with mechanics but still can be largely dependent on your group. Art is great and the shield for the ghost is well crafted. Can take awhile to set up but the experience is worth it.

RATING: 2
I just don't get how this game has become so popular.

A ghost tries to use Dixit cards to tell a bunch of seers about a murder case. Oh it's so creative! Not really. All the ghost can do is pick the least crappy card, and all the seers can do is hope to make the right guess. Not much creativity there.

I'm a much bigger fan of the way the cards are used in Dixit, where you actually get to be creative, making up crazy clues, that can guide the other players on to your twisted train of thought. That part is missing in Mysterium and it just makes it really dull experience.

RATING: 8
Mysterium is a really unique and fun game in which players are playing psychics that have been called to a haunted mansion where a ghost has been haunting the estate ever since his/her murder. The players are there to decipher the dreams that the ghost gives them throughout the night, in order to find the killer, the murder weapon and the location of the murder so the ghost can finally rest in peace.


Pros: entertaining cooperative game,  strong and fun theming, Gorgeous artwork and component quality,Quick gameplay.  High amounts of player interaction, accomadates large player counts.

Cons: Best with larger player counts,  can be difficult to win.no real strategy game play,

RATING: 7.5
This game is fun and different, with very attractive components and art that is tasteful and very functional for the game.  I think anybody who is interested in the concept should definitely try to play it.  One small thing that irked me is that the theme actually doesn't really make sense, something that is only evident when you become familiar with the rules.  Why does the ghost send an incorrect vision to most of the mediums, only guiding one of them towards the truth?  Worse, how can it be that the ghost decides which of these series of visions is correct, and does this only at the final round?!

RATING: N/A
The Dixit-related stuff is my favorite part about Mysterium. The art is really interesting, and it's fun to try and determine why you were given a certain clue by the ghost; was it because of the color, or an object, or a general theme of the picture?

Or maybe the ghost just didn't have very many choices, which is perhaps a drawback of the game, but I would need to play more to know for sure. It's also a somewhat quiet game, it seems, since apparently the ghost isn't supposed to provide feedback or have any discussions. Thematically, perhaps there could have been some sort of communication method back and forth, like the ghost bumping a wall or moving an object or something. I don't know.

It was fine, and I would play it again, since it can be fun in various groups. But I am not currently interested in buying it.

RATING: 7
Really interesting game with a cool premise and mechanics. 

Pros: relatively easy to learn and explain, really engaging art, sturdy pieces, the way you work as a team is fun and listening to how a team interprets the images is entertaining. the game has an awesome theme and overall excellent play experience.

Cons: set up takes forever. FOREVER. so many cards and pieces needed to set up. getting the card's pair is absolutely tedious and keeping piles of cards everywhere is just a mess. i have no idea why weapon cards are so tiny... they either need to make each category a different size or all the cards the same size. the betting mechanic feels... "unnatural" in the sense that everyone has to be reminded each time to place their votes. there's significant amounts of downtime. especially with an overly thoughtful ghost. finally, winning at the end doesn't feel like much of an accomplishment. i guess winning isn't the same if no one loses.

RATING: 2
1 play, 6er

It turns out that I was right: this is NOT my kind of game. At all. I do not speak [i]dream[/i]! Most of the people I played with knew each other so I took their advice early on in trying to interpret the dreams I was being sent. Sadly, in the case of my dreams, they were always wrong. I was the last person to make it to the top -- and even then, it's possible we played an extra round just to get me there. 

So what do I hate about it?
- it's a co-op
- you spend a lot of time sitting around waiting to be given a card
- the cards are very vague ... the whole thing feels very random

The game was vaguely interesting in a ludologic sense -- how they used Dixit tools to craft a game -- but this game is NOT FOR ME.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I bought this based on the glowingly positive Shut Up & Sit Down review and the fact that they keep bring it up every now & then and continue to tout how fun it is. 

For me it's...mediocre. If you want a super-light [b]activity[/b] to do & don't care all that much about strategizing or competitiveness, this could be for you. If you're familiar with Dixit you pretty much know what to expect.

Ultimately, this wasn't for me. I pulled it out once for my regular gaming crew & doubt it would have ever seen the light of day again. I could have kept it until my kids grew old enough to play, but by then something better & more fun will likely exist.

For a game of this length & weight, I'd prefer to play Timeline Challenge. You can play Timeline in teams and everyone is doing the exact same thing. In Mysterium, the ghost [b]cannot[/b] talk to any other players until the game ends. Meh.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
As far as my opinion on the game, see my comments on the Polish version.  These comments are specifically relevant to the content of the American release where it differs from the Polish version.

First of all, hopefully you have played the Polish edition or know someone who has.  If not, download the English rules for that edition and ignore this rulebook entirely.  If I didn't already know how to play the game I would have a really hard time understanding how to play from this rulebook.  It's almost like they expect people to already know how to play because huge chunks of the rules are either omitted or summarized unclearly.  There were a couple times where I went back to the rulebook for a clarification on a small rule to find it nowhere in the rulebook.

On top of that, the rulebook is worth ignoring because the changes between the Polish and the American version are all poor in my opinion.  The major one, which has been addressed by others at length, is the dumb intuition mechanic.  This new mechanic has you voting on whether other players guesses are correct throughout the game and the amount you get right dictates how many of the final 3 cards you actually get to see at the end of the game.  It slows down the game, adds nothing to it, and is counter to a fully cooperative game.  But there are other, smaller, things too that I think are negative changes.  For example, when drawing a new hand in the Polish edition you needed to discard your entire hand.  In the American version you can discard and keep any number of cards.  This takes away from the game, making it a bit too easy, especially if you use this on the final clue set where you have to provide 3 clues from one hand.  Part of the fun and challenge is giving 3 good clues from such limited options and trying to interpret what you're given from those options.  Another is that in the American version the rules tell the ghost to pick the final culprit, that just seems like a silly change.  Picking randomly is much better because it prevents any sort of bias the ghost may have when picking (which if the psychics know the player playing the ghost, might be able to use to influence their decision for better or worse).

So that's a lot of negative stuff but I would still recommend this version over the Polish version every time.  Because the rules are easy to ignore when you can easily obtain the Polish ones but the components in this version are far and away better than the Polish version.  The ghost board especially provides a way to hold, organize, and easily and quickly view all the information.  The player pieces are these attractive plastic crystal balls instead of boring wooden pawns.  The cards are numbered for easy searching and organizing.  The clock that marks the hour (number of turns left) is also an attractive and thematic way to keep track of turns.  The art for all the cards appears to be the same from the Polish version.  If anything, they provide too many nice components as many of them go unused most games and just add to the amount of stuff on the table.  The player envelopes for example, or the crows to keep track of redraws.

So if you like or are interested in this game then this is the version for you.  I would not even venture a look in the rulebook though, just download the English rules for the Polish edition of this game.

RATING: 3
Oh what a game. What a bad, bad game.

You get cards that may or may not have anything to do with the thing you're trying to figure out. If the ghost player has good cards, you can get good cards. In most cases, though, the cards are too abstract to allow for many clever connections and it all just seems random.

The game feels underdeveloped in a couple of areas. One is the voting. Players have vote tokens which they can use to vote on whether or not the other players are right or wrong about their guesses. When you get one correct, you move up on a score track. The score track, in turn, will let you see more secret cards at the end of the game if you're higher on the track. However, you only have to get to about level 7 on the score track to see all of the cards but the track goes all the way to 13. There seems to be some sort of disconnect there as there's no reason keep advanving on the track. There's also a big problem when you get to the final round. At that point the ghost gives three final clue cards which are meant to point to the crime. Again, if the ghost has just one good card then this part is easy. Otherwise, it will be as random as the rest of the game.

This game is even worse than Dixit. At least in Dixit the player gets to choose the clue so there is a chance that somebody will get it. This game removes that one strategic element and makes it come down to random luck of the cards.

As if the game isn't bad enough, then Deception: Murder in Hong Kong came out around the same time. Deception is great and uses a similar system, so there's really no reason to play Mysterium.

RATING: 6
I really wanted to like this game, since I asked it as a Christmas gift and it looked awesome, but the hype and excitement lowered a lot after a few plays. 

Its first problem is the randomness; the murderer is just a random pick at the end between three suspects, so it is not known from the beginning, which messes with the possible "story" about the ghost who wants to tell you who murdered him or her. The combinations of weapon/place/person are also random, which I understand (it is like Cluedo) but they don't offer anything for the story either.

The second problem I found was that it felt to me like a limited Dixit, because the vision/dream cards are just like Dixit ones, but in Dixit there are countless possibilities to interpret them whereas in Mysterium you have to link them to some detail in the suspect cards... and yes there are many, but at the end, for example, if you want to point towards the cook, you will use food elements (if you don't have you will have to be a little more creative, but this is situational), etc.

I still give it a 6 because it is very pretty, I like the Dixit mechanic of making guesses based on artistic cards, and because after some time of not playing it I found some enjoyement on playing it again as a light and fast game... especially as the ghost ! I like to hear other people making guesses about what I picked.

Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 1
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 1
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 5
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 1

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is the English version of the game. Previously I had played the Polish version which is very very similar. Most of the changes in the game are aesthetic. While all the clue cards are the same. The weapon cards, location cards, people cards, and all the card backs are completely redone. With the possible exception of the people cards, all the art seems much better to me.

There's also a lot more stuff with the game. A nifty screen with pouches for the ghost to put cards in... the front of which is absolutely gorgeous. A clock standee thing that counts down the rounds. Ravens that perch on the screen. Cardboard markers that designate the different areas to place the cards. Colored player placards that you give to the ghost, so he can assign cards to players more easily. Crystal ball player pieces. From an artistic/production quality standpoint, this is definitely the version of the game to get.

There are also some rule changes that alter the game slightly. The order in which you solve the crimes is changed, which is a slight difference. There's also a voting mechanic where you can put checks or crosses on other player's guesses to indicate whether you agree or disagree with their choices, although you have a limited supply of those tokens.

If you're right, then you'll get to see more cards at the end of the game when the final murder dream clues are sent. In the final part of the game, one of the sets of people/place/weapon are going to be chosen by the ghost as the actual murder and players will see up to three cards (depending on how well they've judged their partner's guesses) and then vote for which one is right. The combination that gets the most votes is who the team selects. This is the biggest different between the versions. Guessing whether other people are right or not is fun, but I'm not sure I love how it impacts the final part of the game. But there's nothing stopping you from playing the Polish rules.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
About [thing=181304][/thing]:

[b]1) What is it?[/b]
[thing=181304][/thing] is [thing=1294][/thing] meets [thing=39856][/thing]. Players are mediums that receive dreams from a Ghost (the clue giver), in order to solve a murder in the house in which it occured. The dreams are cards - in [thing=39856][/thing] style (ie: weird and beautiful, with lots of possible interpretations) - that the Ghost send to them. Every player has a set previously made of Suspect/Place/Weapon, that they must discover in the time given. If everyone manages to discover their set, a final round will happen, in which the Mediums will have to uncover which set is the true one.

This is basically it. [thing=181304][/thing] has simple rules and is very easy to learn. Playing time do fits around the purposed 42 minutes, even when having a full table (7 players), but it gets shorter with less, as even with some of the game being simultaneous, when the Ghost give clues, the less she has to give, faster it is.

The game allows for cooperation, as players can help others in trying to "crack the code" of the messages and understand the meaning of them.

Overall, [thing=181304][/thing] provides a fun enviroment (with room for light banter - "what do you mean with this??"), with some tension (not much, but there is a timer, which always put pressure in decisions) and team work, all in a gorgeous package, with a short playing time.

[b]2) How do you play?[/b]
After the set up, the Ghost player make random sets, among the cards used, and pair them with each player - this is the first goal of the Mediums players, but they don't have this information, of course.

All the medium players have Right/Wrong tokens, which they can use in the guesses of other players, accordingly to what they think - when they are correct, they advance on the track.

Players receive clue cards in order to guess first the Suspect, then the Place and finally the Weapon. If the player can't guess right on the first chance, they keep the card or cards received, and will receive more in the next round.

After every player received their clues, the time to guess starts. Players must use their Right/Wrong tokens also inside this time. Once the time runs out, the Ghost player announces who was right and who was wrong. The ones that got it right, advance to uncover the next piece of of information - the Place. The ones that didn't, stay to find the Suspect. 

The clock advances 1 hour and a new round begins. Now the Ghost will give clues accordingly to the spot players are (so, she will give clues regarding Suspect for those still to find theirs, and Places, for those already there). This will continue until one or more players discover the three things they needed. These players will advance on the track 7 minus the Current Hour in spaces (so, the sooner, the better). After this, these players will still be able to help the others behind to uncover their sets, but will no longer receive clues themselves.

Finally, if everyone uncover all the needed informations, the final round will begin. The Ghost will select three cards, one to represent the Murderer, one for the Place and one for the Weapon - all of these three things will belong to just one of the sets the players uncovered. However, not everyone might be able to look at all the three selected cards before taking a guess about which is the correct set - this is decided by the place on the track the player is. The further, the best - that is why reaching the end soon and/or using well the Right/Wrong tokens count. Once everyone has chosen their guess about the correct set, the guesses are revealed and the set with the most votes will be the one selected. If the set is indeed the proper one, players win! If not, they lose.

Players also lose if the time runs out (7 rounds) and there are still someone who haven't discovered all the needed informations.

[b]3) Which are the decisions made during play?[/b]
For the Ghost there are more decisions: which card or cards to send to each person. This is indeed the hardest part of the game. Not truly "hard", but sure can be tough.

For the Mediums, it is just a matter to see the clues and take informed guesses - both to find their own things, and also to use their Right/Wrong tokens. While understanding the clues can be a tough nut to crack, the decisions on themselves are rather easy and can even be left for chance.

[b]4) What are the good things in the game?[/b]
- Beautiful production - both for the components and the art;
- Easy to play;
- Quick playing time;
- While others can help you with the clues, the decision is personal, so there is little room for alpha players;
- Language independant.

[b]5) Which are the bad news?[/b]
- Not everyone will want to play in the Ghost espectral shoes, so the position can be left several times with the same person, which can be a bummer;
- Due to the open nature of the clues and guesses, the game can frustrate players that like more control and objectivity;
- The added pressure of the hourglass doesn't fit well with everyone;
- There can be some downtime while waiting for the Ghost to give out clues.

[b]6) How do you feel while playing?[/b]
Like playing Wraith: the Oblivion, without all the drama and with added colors. When playing Wraith we, sometimes, had to pass information to persons alive. Maybe an Espectre threatened them, or someone was robbing them, or even something as simply as reminding your wife to read a bed time story to your kid. The work of a bounded wraith is hard, though, so we had to use the little we had with a lot of cost in pathos. And almost all the time it went wrong.

Normal people simply aren't ready to deal with messages from beyond the shroud. But there are the Mediums - like Oda Mae Brown, from Ghost. They not only could hear better, they also, usually, don't freak out completely when a wraith spoke or wrote to them. Still, that doesn't mean they would understand our meaning - just that most wouldn't faint, die or eat pills to end the whispers. Again, the job of a vengeful ghost is hard. It seemed so simple to us!

Well, [thing=181304][/thing] makes the job of the Ghost a constant roller coaster of emotions, usually going from elation, of having a clue hit home, to utter frustration, of many losing their mark, even when they are as clear as possible, because one picture of a jungle full of dangers has a tiny image of a boat, so of course you meant the Sailor and not the Explorer. It makes sense! Now imagine that you, as a Ghost, truly wanted to do precisely this, because that was the only freaking card with a ship or even a sea on it!

Therefore, the guessing work for the Mediums isn't truly a piece of cake all the time. Sometimes you are 100% sure of something, only to discover that, well, 100% sure is one of the most assured ways to be wrong. This happens because the Ghost [i]must[/i] send clues, even when she doesn't want to, because no card has a good connection to what she wants you to see, and, worst, they can send you off the track. It is usual that Mediums who made one of two wrong guesses to have conflicting clues in front of them, which can be exasperating. And in this is the fun of the game - otherwise it would be too easy and direct to be worth the trouble.

In the end, [thing=181304][/thing] fulfilled what I expected of it: a quick and fun game, with little to worry about and with some banter and laughs spread across the play. I recommend it.

- Quickly needs the extra cards from the expansion to stay fresh.

RATING: 6
I don't like cooperative games but this one is different, it plays a lot faster than they usually do.
For every player, there is a crime “scenario“ fixed and you try to find out your murderer, scene and weapon, each time with the help of the ghost player (which knows everything). This is a very fun and unique aspect of the game.
It has some parallels to Deception but is way better because you really get close to being sure whether you're right or wrong (not the case in Deception).
The big pity is that you only win together which is just boring.
But all in all a good game, recommend it.

RATING: 6
My observation that I don't really enjoy Dixit/AtA/CAH style games remains true. I generally enjoy trying to interpret what other other people are thinking but I seem to always either overthink or underthink it. 

The game around Mysterium is interesting, but it was VERY confusing for me to decipher my goals every time. Was I guessing the murderer? Am I guessing the victim? Murder weapon? Why does everyone have their own guess that's different? I think that, theme-wise, this confused me and made the game harder than it needed to be. 

I'd play again, and I might like being the ghost even more than a player, but it's certainly not a game I'd request.

I could see that the amount of fun you have probably depends on the players. I really enjoyed it - it's a good mental challenge, requiring a lot of analysis and thought and creativity but without strategy. A+.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Mysterium is such a neat abstract game to play. First time I saw it being played I was immediately drawn in by the gameplay and the theme of it.

You have your group playing a ghost who hands out picture cards as clues for the ghost detectives guess which card is associated with the dream card they received to advance through 3 stages/levels to find out who the killer is.

It's so much fun, playing as the ghost it's so much fun trying to figure out which dream to give to the right player, and hearing what their thought process is in deciding what message you're trying to convey to hint them to a card.
As a ghost detective it feels so satisfying when you figure what the ghost is trying to tell you and also hilarious facepalm when your intuition is wrong.

I do recommend at least checking out the game.

If there's any negatives is I would say replayability is not as replayable as I might have thought it'd be with the number of cards(But I might just need to play on the more difficult settings to see a difference), but there are expansions that give more cards to use so that might help.

RATING: 8
Nice game that does really well within my gaming group. Really easy to teach to people who are already familiar to Dixit, yet easy enough to teach to anyone. I like both being the Ghost and the investigator.

I don't really like the ending part of the game, where the Ghost decides upon a murder that all investigators have to guess based on a number of cards they are allowed to see. I do like the voting part the comes to the table, so I can see some value. I just don't like the finale to be honest... Is the most boring part for me as investigator (it's okey as Ghost)

RATING: 8
An amazing experience. Although the long replay-ability might wain over time as people become accustomed to the cards (my only complaint). This looks gorgeous on the table, oozes cooperative play, is stuffed with gobs of theme and is still fairly simple to play. I love being the Ghost more than the psychic detectives, but I'll do either side. Perfect gateway game, this is what Clue wishes it could be. Basically its a cooperative twist on one versus many. Its One who is "dead" which means I have all the answers and must give you abstract art cards as clues versus the rest of my team who must figure out said clues and deduce who killed me, with what, and where. Everyone should own this game.

Artwork- 10/10
Theme- 10/10
Mechanics- 9/10
Fun- 8/10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Mysterium is constantly teetering on the edge for me on whether I like it or not. The Clue x Dixit love child idea is a clever one, although in practice has a couple of flaws. 

First is the downtime. One player has to study an array of cards and can take his sweet time, and this gets worse with more players. If you're not the ghost, you're just waiting most of the time. 

Secondly, you have to see the cards well. You have to study all of them meticulously, and with bad lighting or with 6 others crammed around a table, this can be quite a challenge.

RATING: 10
A co-op game for 2-7 players. One player is the ghost, unable to speak, trying to get the other plays to guess their assigned suspect, location, and weapon cards. The ghost can only communicate by giving the other players abstract, dream like art cards.

RATING: 7
A great deduction-game with supernice artwork. I would say this works for families and gamers alike.
The description of Cluedo plus Dixit is really true, but the gameplay is much better as in Cluedo. All the players are trying to figure out their mystery at the same time and can even help each other, the vision-track and the reveal at the end add a nice bit of competition and the player screen makes playing as the ghost feel really cool.
I would definitely recommend this over Cluedo if you are looking for a murder-mystery game.

RATING: N/A
6.5 after 1 play

Mildly intriguing and thematic gameplay and coupled with good artwork and substantial player interaction. However, it may not be suitable with a group of strangers, and is more suited for friends, as clues will need some familiarity with the player taking on the ghost role. Indeed, the enjoyment of the game is heavily dependent on the ghost role, e.g. how good the clues are and amount of downtime.

The game has nice artwork and good quality components. However, some of it seems over-produced, e.g. the crow markers and very tall game screen.

Dixit with a purpose is an overused but accurate description of this game.  I like studying the neat artwork looking for links between images and found the group deduction to be quite enjoyable.  I was less keen on the scoring system, but it seemed to work okay.  We also played with the easiest setup so perhaps I'd like it even more with more restrictions in play.  Not something I need to add to my collection... but if I wanted a new deduction game this would probably be it.

RATING: 8
Takes the madness that is dixit and builds a fantastic cooperative game on top.  Can occasionally be very stressful and the points for voting system is sometimes a little counter-intuitive (at certain player counts, everyone guessing correctly all the time is actually bad for the final round).
Even so, I've never had a game of this which the players didn't enjoy.

RATING: 9.5
Érdekes és nagyon hangulatos volt. Megfelelő társasággal van benne erő, de otthonra nem kéne, két fővel nekem ez esélytelen. Egy beszélgetős-borozgatós-félhomályos házibulin azért szívesen játszanám többször.
---
Nagyon jó partijáték, ha rendszeresen össze tudtuk ülni minimum 3-an, akkor kötelező vétel, nagyon megéri az árát!
7 -> 9
---
Csak sikerült rábeszélni magam. Baráti és családi összejövetelek egész ősszel-télen (szülinapok, karácsony, szilveszter), megéri még ezen ritka alkalmakra is az árát.
---
Lecseréltem a pimpelt változatra. A paraván miatt kap még fél pontot, sokkal szebb így az élet.

That makes this game super boring for everyone except for the ghost that is in action all the time, cause he is rushing to give clues.
